Based on this\n    49→  /// value, you can cast to a class defined in DerivedTypes.h.\n    50→  /// Note: If you add an element to this, you need to add an element to the\n    51→  /// Type::getPrimitiveType function, or else things will break!\n    52→  /// Also update LLVMTypeKind and LLVMGetTypeKind () in the C binding.\n    53→  ///\n    54→  enum TypeID {\n    55→    // PrimitiveTypes\n    56→    HalfTyID = 0,  ///< 16-bit floating point type\n    57→    BFloatTyID,    ///< 16-bit floating point type (7-bit significand)\n    58→    FloatTyID,     ///< 32-bit floating point type\n    59→    DoubleTyID,    ///< 64-bit floating point type\n    60→    X86_FP80TyID,  ///< 80-bit floating point type (X87)\n    61→    FP128TyID,     ///< 128-bit floating point type (112-bit significand)\n    62→    PPC_FP128TyID, ///< 128-bit floating point type (two 64-bits, PowerPC)\n    63→    VoidTyID,      ///< type with no size\n    64→    LabelTyID,     ///< Labels\n    65→    MetadataTyID,  ///< Metadata\n    66→    X86_AMXTyID,   ///< AMX vectors (8192 bits, X86 specific)\n    67→    TokenTyID,     ///< Tokens\n    68→\n    69→    // Derived types... see DerivedTypes.h file.\n    70→    IntegerTyID,        ///< Arbitrary bit width integers\n    71→    FunctionTyID,       ///< Functions\n    72→    PointerTyID,        ///< Pointers\n    73→    StructTyID,         ///< Structures\n    74→    ArrayTyID,          ///< Arrays\n    75→    FixedVectorTyID,    ///< Fixed width SIMD vector type\n    76→    ScalableVectorTyID, ///< Scalable SIMD vector type\n    77→    TypedPointerTyID,   ///< Typed pointer used by some GPU targets\n    78→    TargetExtTyID,      ///< Target extension type\n    79→  };\n    80→\n    81→private:\n    82→  /// This refers to the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n    83→  LLVMContext &Context;\n    84→\n    85→  TypeID   ID : 8;            // The current base type of this type.\n    86→  unsigned SubclassData : 24; // Space for subclasses to store data.\n    87→                              // Note that this should be synchronized with\n    88→                              // MAX_INT_BITS value in IntegerType class.\n    89→\n    90→protected:\n    91→  friend class LLVMContextImpl;\n    92→\n    93→  explicit Type(LLVMContext &C, TypeID tid)\n    94→    : Context(C), ID(tid), SubclassData(0) {}\n    95→  ~Type() = default;\n    96→\n    97→  unsigned getSubclassData() const { return SubclassData; }\n    98→\n    99→  void setSubclassData(unsigned val) {\n   100→    SubclassData = val;\n   101→    // Ensure we don't have any accidental truncation.\n   102→    assert(getSubclassData() == val && \"Subclass data too large for field\");\n   103→  }\n   104→\n   105→  /// Keeps track of how many Type*'s there are in the ContainedTys list.\n   106→  unsigned NumContainedTys = 0;\n   107→\n   108→  /// A pointer to the array of Types contained by this Type. For example, this\n   109→  /// includes the arguments of a function type, the elements of a structure,\n   110→  /// the pointee of a pointer, the element type of an array, etc. This pointer\n   111→  /// may be 0 for types that don't contain other types (Integer, Double,\n   112→  /// Float).\n   113→  Type * const *ContainedTys = nullptr;\n   114→\n   115→public:\n   116→  /// Print the current type.\n   117→  /// Omit the type details if \\p NoDetails == true.\n   118→  /// E.g., let %st = type { i32, i16 }\n   119→  /// When \\p NoDetails is true, we only print %st.\n   120→  /// Put differently, \\p NoDetails prints the type as if\n   121→  /// inlined with the operands when printing an instruction.\n   122→  LLVM_ABI void print(raw_ostream &O, bool IsForDebug = false,\n   123→                      bool NoDetails = false) const;\n   124→\n   125→  LLVM_ABI void dump() const;\n   126→\n   127→  /// Return the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n   128→  LLVMContext &getContext() const { return Context; }\n   129→\n   130→  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n   131→  // Accessors for working with types.\n   132→  //\n   133→\n   134→  /// Return the type id for the type. This will return one of the TypeID enum\n   135→  /// elements defined above.\n   136→  TypeID getTypeID() const { return ID; }\n   137→\n   138→  /// Return true if this is 'void'.\n   139→  bool isVoidTy() const { return getTypeID() == VoidTyID; }\n   140→\n   141→  /// Return true if this is 'half', a 16-bit IEEE fp type.\n   142→  bool isHalfTy() const { return getTypeID() == HalfTyID; }\n   143→\n   144→  /// Return true if this is 'bfloat', a 16-bit bfloat type.\n   145→  bool isBFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID; }\n   146→\n   147→  /// Return true if this is a 16-bit float type.\n   148→  bool is16bitFPTy() const {\n   149→    return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID || getTypeID() == HalfTyID;\n   150→  }\n   151→\n   152→  /// Return true if this is 'float', a 32-bit IEEE fp type.\n   153→  bool isFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == FloatTyID; }\n   154→\n   155→  /// Return true if this is 'double', a 64-bit IEEE fp type.\n   156→  bool isDoubleTy() const { return getTypeID() == DoubleTyID; }\n   157→\n   158→  /// Return true if this is x86 long double.\n   159→  bool isX86_FP80Ty() const { return getTypeID() == X86_FP80TyID; }\n   160→\n   161→  /// Return true if this is 'fp128'.\n   162→  bool isFP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == FP128TyID; }\n   163→\n   164→  /// Return true if this is powerpc long double.\n   165→  bool isPPC_FP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID; }\n   166→\n   167→  /// Return true if this is a well-behaved IEEE-like type, which has a IEEE\n   168→  /// compatible layout, and does not have non-IEEE values, such as x86_fp80's\n   169→  /// unnormal values.\n   170→  bool isIEEELikeFPTy() const {\n   171→    switch (getTypeID()) {\n   172→    case DoubleTyID:\n   173→    case FloatTyID:\n   174→    case HalfTyID:\n   175→    case BFloatTyID:\n   176→    case FP128TyID:\n   177→      return true;\n   178→    default:\n   179→      return false;\n   180→    }\n   181→  }\n   182→\n   183→  /// Return true if this is one of the floating-point types\n   184→  bool isFloatingPointTy() const {\n   185→    return isIEEELikeFPTy() || getTypeID() == X86_FP80TyID ||\n   186→           getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\n   187→  }\n   188→\n   189→  /// Returns true if this is a floating-point type that is an unevaluated sum\n   190→  /// of multiple floating-point units.\n   191→  /// An example of such a type is ppc_fp128, also known as double-double, which\n   192→  /// consists of two IEEE 754 doubles.\n   193→  bool isMultiUnitFPType() const {\n   194→    return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\n   195→  }\n   196→\n   197→  LLVM_ABI const fltSemantics &getFltSemantics() const;\n   198→\n   199→  /// Return true if this is X86 AMX.\n   200→  bool isX86_AMXTy() const { return getTypeID() == X86_AMXTyID; To get the\n   309→  /// actual size for a particular target, it is reasonable to use the\n   310→  /// DataLayout subsystem to do this.\n   311→  bool isSized(SmallPtrSetImpl<Type*> *Visited = nullptr) const {\n   312→    // If it's a primitive, it is always sized.\n   313→    if (getTypeID() == IntegerTyID || isFloatingPointTy() ||\n   314→        getTypeID() == PointerTyID || getTypeID() == X86_AMXTyID)\n   315→      return true;\n   316→    // If it is not something that can have a size (e.g. a function or label),\n   317→    // it doesn't have a size.\n   318→    if (getTypeID() != StructTyID && getTypeID() != ArrayTyID &&\n   319→        !isVectorTy() && getTypeID() != TargetExtTyID)\n   320→      return false;\n   321→    // Otherwise we have to try harder to decide.\n   322→    return isSizedDerivedType(Visited);\n   323→  }\n   324→\n   325→  /// Return the basic size of this type if it is a primitive type. For more \"Type\"\n// stuff, look in DerivedTypes.h.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_IR_TYPE_H\n#define LLVM_IR_TYPE_H\n\n#include \"llvm/ADT/ArrayRef.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/CBindingWrapping.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Casting.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/ErrorHandling.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/TypeSize.h\"\n#include <cassert>\n#include <cstdint>\n#include <iterator>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\nclass IntegerType;\nstruct fltSemantics;\nclass LLVMContext;\nclass PointerType;\nclass raw_ostream;\nclass StringRef;\ntemplate <typename PtrType> class SmallPtrSetImpl;\n\n/// The instances of the Type class are immutable: once they are created,\n/// they are never changed.  Also note that only one instance of a particular\n/// type is ever created.  Thus seeing if two types are equal is a matter of\n/// doing a trivial pointer comparison. To enforce that no two equal instances\n/// are created, Type instances can only be created via static factory methods\n/// in class Type and in derived classes.  Once allocated, Types are never\n/// free'd.\n///\nclass Type {\npublic:\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  /// Definitions of all of the base types for the Type system.  Based on this\n  /// value, you can cast to a class defined in DerivedTypes.h.\n  /// Note: If you add an element to this, you need to add an element to the\n  /// Type::getPrimitiveType function, or else things will break!\n  /// Also update LLVMTypeKind and LLVMGetTypeKind () in the C binding.\n  ///\n  enum TypeID {\n    // PrimitiveTypes\n    HalfTyID = 0,  ///< 16-bit floating point type\n    BFloatTyID,    ///< 16-bit floating point type (7-bit significand)\n    FloatTyID,     ///< 32-bit floating point type\n    DoubleTyID,    ///< 64-bit floating point type\n    X86_FP80TyID,  ///< 80-bit floating point type (X87)\n    FP128TyID,     ///< 128-bit floating point type (112-bit significand)\n    PPC_FP128TyID, ///< 128-bit floating point type (two 64-bits, PowerPC)\n    VoidTyID,      ///< type with no size\n    LabelTyID,     ///< Labels\n    MetadataTyID,  ///< Metadata\n    X86_AMXTyID,   ///< AMX vectors (8192 bits, X86 specific)\n    TokenTyID,     ///< Tokens\n\n    // Derived types... see DerivedTypes.h file.\n    IntegerTyID,        ///< Arbitrary bit width integers\n    FunctionTyID,       ///< Functions\n    PointerTyID,        ///< Pointers\n    StructTyID,         ///< Structures\n    ArrayTyID,          ///< Arrays\n    FixedVectorTyID,    ///< Fixed width SIMD vector type\n    ScalableVectorTyID, ///< Scalable SIMD vector type\n    TypedPointerTyID,   ///< Typed pointer used by some GPU targets\n    TargetExtTyID,      ///< Target extension type\n  };\n\nprivate:\n  /// This refers to the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n  LLVMContext &Context;\n\n  TypeID   ID : 8;            // The current base type of this type.\n  unsigned SubclassData : 24; // Space for subclasses to store data.\n                              // Note that this should be synchronized with\n                              // MAX_INT_BITS value in IntegerType class.\n\nprotected:\n  friend class LLVMContextImpl;\n\n  explicit Type(LLVMContext &C, TypeID tid)\n    : Context(C), ID(tid), SubclassData(0) {}\n  ~Type() = default;\n\n  unsigned getSubclassData() const { return SubclassData; }\n\n  void setSubclassData(unsigned val) {\n    SubclassData = val;\n    // Ensure we don't have any accidental truncation.\n    assert(getSubclassData() == val && \"Subclass data too large for field\");\n  }\n\n  /// Keeps track of how many Type*'s there are in the ContainedTys list.\n  unsigned NumContainedTys = 0;\n\n  /// A pointer to the array of Types contained by this Type. For example, this\n  /// includes the arguments of a function type, the elements of a structure,\n  /// the pointee of a pointer, the element type of an array, etc. This pointer\n  /// may be 0 for types that don't contain other types (Integer, Double,\n  /// Float).\n  Type * const *ContainedTys = nullptr;\n\npublic:\n  /// Print the current type.\n  /// Omit the type details if \\p NoDetails == true.\n  /// E.g., let %st = type { i32, i16 }\n  /// When \\p NoDetails is true, we only print %st.\n  /// Put differently, \\p NoDetails prints the type as if\n  /// inlined with the operands when printing an instruction.\n  LLVM_ABI void print(raw_ostream &O, bool IsForDebug = false,\n                      bool NoDetails = false) const;\n\n  LLVM_ABI void dump() const;\n\n  /// Return the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n  LLVMContext &getContext() const { return Context; }\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // Accessors for working with types.\n  //\n\n  /// Return the type id for the type. This will return one of the TypeID enum\n  /// elements defined above.\n  TypeID getTypeID() const { return ID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'void'.\n  bool isVoidTy() const { return getTypeID() == VoidTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'half', a 16-bit IEEE fp type.\n  bool isHalfTy() const { return getTypeID() == HalfTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'bfloat', a 16-bit bfloat type.\n  bool isBFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a 16-bit float type.\n  bool is16bitFPTy() const {\n    return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID || getTypeID() == HalfTyID;\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'float', a 32-bit IEEE fp type.\n  bool isFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == FloatTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'double', a 64-bit IEEE fp type.\n  bool isDoubleTy() const { return getTypeID() == DoubleTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is x86 long double.\n  bool isX86_FP80Ty() const { return getTypeID() == X86_FP80TyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'fp128'.\n  bool isFP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == FP128TyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is powerpc long double.\n  bool isPPC_FP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a well-behaved IEEE-like type, which has a IEEE\n  /// compatible layout, and does not have non-IEEE values, such as x86_fp80's\n  /// unnormal values.\n  bool isIEEELikeFPTy() const {\n    switch (getTypeID()) {\n    case DoubleTyID:\n    case FloatTyID:\n    case HalfTyID:\n    case BFloatTyID:\n    case FP128TyID:\n      return true;\n    default:\n      return false;\n    }\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is one of the floating-point types\n  bool isFloatingPointTy() const {\n    return isIEEELikeFPTy() || getTypeID() == X86_FP80TyID ||\n           getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\n  }\n\n  /// Returns true if this is a floating-point type that is an unevaluated sum\n  /// of multiple floating-point units.\n  /// An example of such a type is ppc_fp128, also known as double-double, which\n  /// consists of two IEEE 754 doubles.\n  bool isMultiUnitFPType() const {\n    return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\n  }\n\n  LLVM_ABI const fltSemantics &getFltSemantics() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is X86 AMX.\n  bool isX86_AMXTy() const { return getTypeID() == X86_AMXTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a target extension type.\n  bool isTargetExtTy() const { return getTypeID() == TargetExtTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a target extension type with a scalable layout.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTargetExtTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is a type whose size is a known multiple of vscale.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTy(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type is or contains a target extension type that\n  /// disallows being used as a global.\n  LLVM_ABI bool\n  containsNonGlobalTargetExtType(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n  LLVM_ABI bool containsNonGlobalTargetExtType() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type is or contains a target extension type that\n  /// disallows being used as a local.\n  LLVM_ABI bool\n  containsNonLocalTargetExtType(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n  LLVM_ABI bool containsNonLocalTargetExtType() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is a FP type or a vector of FP.\n  bool isFPOrFPVectorTy() const { return getScalarType()->isFloatingPointTy(); }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'label'.\n  bool isLabelTy() const { return getTypeID() == LabelTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'metadata'.\n  bool isMetadataTy() const { return getTypeID() == MetadataTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'token'.\n  bool isTokenTy() const { return getTypeID() == TokenTyID; }\n\n  /// Returns true if this is 'token' or a token-like target type.s\n  LLVM_ABI bool isTokenLikeTy() const;\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of IntegerType.\n  bool isIntegerTy() const { return getTypeID() == IntegerTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is an IntegerType of the given width.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isIntegerTy(unsigned Bitwidth) const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is an integer type or a vector of integer types.\n  bool isIntOrIntVectorTy() const { return getScalarType()->isIntegerTy(); }\n\n  /// Return true if this is an integer type or a vector of integer types of\n  /// the given width.\n  bool isIntOrIntVectorTy(unsigned BitWidth) const {\n    return getScalarType()->isIntegerTy(BitWidth);\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is an integer type or a pointer type.\n  bool isIntOrPtrTy() const { return isIntegerTy() || isPointerTy(); }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of FunctionType.\n  bool isFunctionTy() const { return getTypeID() == FunctionTyID; }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of StructType.\n  bool isStructTy() const { return getTypeID() == StructTyID; }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of ArrayType.\n  bool isArrayTy() const { return getTypeID() == ArrayTyID; }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of PointerType.\n  bool isPointerTy() const { return getTypeID() == PointerTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a pointer type or a vector of pointer types.\n  bool isPtrOrPtrVectorTy() const { return getScalarType()->isPointerTy(); }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of VectorType.\n  inline bool isVectorTy() const {\n    return getTypeID() == ScalableVectorTyID || getTypeID() == FixedVectorTyID;\n  }\n\n  // True if this is an instance of TargetExtType of RISC-V vector tuple.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isRISCVVectorTupleTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type could be converted with a lossless BitCast to\n  /// type 'Ty'. For example, i8* to i32*. BitCasts are valid for types of the\n  /// same size only where no re-interpretation of the bits is done.\n  /// Determine if this type could be losslessly bitcast to Ty\n  LLVM_ABI bool canLosslesslyBitCastTo(Type *Ty) const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type is empty, that is, it has no elements or all of\n  /// its elements are empty.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isEmptyTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if the type is \"first class\", meaning it is a valid type for a\n  /// Value.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isFirstClassType() const;\n\n  /// Return true if the type is a valid type for a register in codegen. This\n  /// includes all first-class types except struct and array types.\n  bool isSingleValueType() const {\n    return isFloatingPointTy() || isIntegerTy() || isPointerTy() ||\n           isVectorTy() || isX86_AMXTy() || isTargetExtTy();\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if the type is an aggregate type. This means it is valid as\n  /// the first operand of an insertvalue or extractvalue instruction. This\n  /// includes struct and array types, but does not include vector types.\n  bool isAggregateType() const {\n    return getTypeID() == StructTyID || getTypeID() == ArrayTyID;\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if it makes sense to take the size of this type. To get the\n  /// actual size for a particular target, it is reasonable to use the\n  /// DataLayout subsystem to do this.\n  bool isSized(SmallPtrSetImpl<Type*> *Visited = nullptr) const {\n    // If it's a primitive, it is always sized.\n    if (getTypeID() == IntegerTyID || isFloatingPointTy() ||\n        getTypeID() == PointerTyID || getTypeID() == X86_AMXTyID)\n      return true;\n    // If it is not something that can have a size (e.g. a function or label),\n    // it doesn't have a size.\n    if (getTypeID() != StructTyID && getTypeID() != ArrayTyID &&\n        !isVectorTy() && getTypeID() != TargetExtTyID)\n      return false;\n    // Otherwise we have to try harder to decide.\n    return isSizedDerivedType(Visited);\n  }\n\n  /// Return the basic size of this type if it is a primitive type. If the FP type does not have a stable mantissa (e.g.\n  /// ppc long double), this method returns -1.\n  LLVM_ABI int getFPMantissaWidth() const;\n\n  /// If this is a vector type, return the element type, otherwise return\n  /// 'this'.\n  inline Type *getScalarType() const {\n    if (isVectorTy())\n      return getContainedType(0);\n    return const_cast<Type *>(this);\n  }\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // Type Iteration support.\n  //\n  using subtype_iterator = Type * const *;\n\n  subtype_iterator subtype_begin() const { return ContainedTys; }\n  subtype_iterator subtype_end() const { return &ContainedTys[NumContainedTys];}\n  ArrayRef<Type*> subtypes() const {\n    return ArrayRef(subtype_begin(), subtype_end());\n  }\n\n  using subtype_reverse_iterator = std::reverse_iterator<subtype_iterator>;\n\n  subtype_reverse_iterator subtype_rbegin() const {\n    return subtype_reverse_iterator(subtype_end());\n  }\n  subtype_reverse_iterator subtype_rend() const {\n    return subtype_reverse_iterator(subtype_begin());\n  }\n\n  /// This method is used to implement the type iterator (defined at the end of\n  /// the file). For vectors, preserves element count.\n  LLVM_ABI inline Type *getExtendedType() const;\n\n  /// Get the address space of this pointer or pointer vector type.\n  LLVM_ABI inline unsigned getPointerAddressSpace() const;\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // Static members exported by the Type class itself.  Useful for getting\n  // instances of Type.\n  //\n\n  /// Return a type based on an identifier.\n  LLVM_ABI static Type *getPrimitiveType(LLVMContext &C, TypeID IDNumber);\n\n All\n    85→  /// operand bundle tags that LLVM has special knowledge of are listed here.\n    86→  /// Additionally, this scheme allows LLVM to efficiently check for specific\n    87→  /// operand bundle tags without comparing strings. Keep this in sync with\n    88→  /// LLVMContext::LLVMContext().\n    89→  enum : unsigned {\n    90→    OB_deopt = 0,                  // \"deopt\"\n    91→    OB_funclet = 1,                // \"funclet\"\n    92→    OB_gc_transition = 2,          // \"gc-transition\"\n    93→    OB_cfguardtarget = 3,          // \"cfguardtarget\"\n    94→    OB_preallocated = 4,           // \"preallocated\"\n    95→    OB_gc_live = 5,                // \"gc-live\"\n    96→    OB_clang_arc_attachedcall = 6, // \"clang.arc.attachedcall\"\n    97→    OB_ptrauth = 7,                // \"ptrauth\"\n    98→    OB_kcfi = 8,                   // \"kcfi\"\n    99→    OB_convergencectrl = 9,        // \"convergencectrl\"\n   100→    OB_align = 10,                 // \"align\"\n   101→    OB_deactivation_symbol = 11,   // \"deactivation-symbol\"\n   102→    OB_LastBundleID = OB_deactivation_symbol\n   103→  };\n   104→\n   105→  /// getMDKindID - Return a unique non-zero ID for the specified metadata kind.\n   106→  /// This ID is uniqued across modules in the current LLVMContext.\n   107→  LLVM_ABI unsigned getMDKindID(StringRef Name) const;\n   108→\n   109→  /// getMDKindNames - Populate client supplied SmallVector with the name for\n   110→  /// custom metadata IDs registered in this LLVMContext.\n   111→  LLVM_ABI void getMDKindNames(SmallVectorImpl<StringRef> &Result) const;\n   112→\n   113→  /// getOperandBundleTags - Populate client supplied SmallVector with the\n   114→  /// bundle tags registered in this LLVMContext. The function pattern-matches on Type::TypeID:\\n   - IntegerType → EVT::getIntegerVT(Context, BitWidth)\\n   - VectorType → EVT::getVectorVT(Context, ElementEVT, ElementCount)\\n   - PointerType → Handled separately in TargetLowering\\n   - Falls back to MVT::getVT() for primitive types\\n\\n2. **TargetLowering::getValueType()** (llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h:1740): Higher-level API that wraps EVT::getEVT with target-specific handling:\\n   - Converts scalar pointers to native pointer types (getPointerTy)\\n   - Converts vector element types\\n   - Returns EVT (which can represent both simple MVT and extended types)\\n   - getSimpleValueType() (line 1781) further converts to machine-native MVT\\n\\n3. **DAGTypeLegalizer** (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeTypes.h:31): Implements type legalization for code generation:\\n   - Stores ValueTypeActions from TargetLowering for each EVT\\n   - getTypeAction() (line 62) queries TLI::getTypeAction() to determine if type is Legal, Promote, Split, or Expand\\n   - Contains maps for tracking promoted, split, and expanded types (lines 98-100+)\\n   - LegalizeTypes.cpp implements specialized legalization for different type categories\\n\\n## Summary of Data Flow\\n\\n```\\nType Creation → LLVMContext (owns types) → LLVMContextImpl (uniquing tables)\\n                                  ↓\\nIR Type (IntegerType/FunctionType/StructType) \\n                                  ↓\\nEVT::getEVT(Type*) → Extended Value Type\\n                                  ↓\\nTargetLowering::getValueType(DataLayout, Type*) → machine-specific EVT/MVT\\n                                  ↓\\nDAGTypeLegalizer::getTypeAction(EVT) → Legal/Promote/Split/Expand decision\\n                                  ↓\\nLegalizeTypes.cpp → Machine IR with legal types\\n```\"\n}\n","numLines":44,"startLine":1,"totalLines":44}}}
